  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d1d9e2be-8230-4e83-8785-79c5400d80dc'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer1230998184007851459">After the shocking ending of <i>The Everafter War</i>, this book picks up with Sabrina, Daphne, and Puck stuck in the Book of Everafter, where all the fairy tales are stored and enchanted characters can change their destinies. The girls (and Puck) must chase the Master through a series of stories, where they’re willing to change what they need in order to save their baby brother.</span>
  <span id="freeText1230998184007851459" style="display:none">After the shocking ending of <i>The Everafter War</i>, this book picks up with Sabrina, Daphne, and Puck stuck in the Book of Everafter, where all the fairy tales are stored and enchanted characters can change their destinies. The girls (and Puck) must chase the Master through a series of stories, where they’re willing to change what they need in order to save their baby brother. Soon, however, they are confronted by the Editor—the book’s guardian—who, along with an army of tiny monsters known as Revisers, threatens the children with dire consequences if they don’t stick to the stories. As they chase their quarry and dodge the Revisers, they meet Alice, Mowgli, Jack the Giant Killer, Hansel and Gretel, the Headless Horseman, and more. But will they find their brother in time?<br /><br /><br />F&amp;P level: U</span>

<div id="review_242847618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/242847618" />
    <a title="Charissa Sophia de la Rosa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7108558-charissa-sophia-de-la-rosa"><img alt="Charissa Sophia de la Rosa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398029499p2/7108558.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/242847618?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charissa Sophia de la Rosa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charissa Sophia de la Rosa" href="/user/show/7108558-charissa-sophia-de-la-rosa">Charissa Sophia de la Rosa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7108558-charissa-sophia-de-la-rosa?shelf=books-by-my-favorite-authors">books-by-my-favorite-authors</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer242847618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1148484311727023957">Ok, I have only one word to say about this book: Outstanding. First, there are a lot of suspense and thrilling moments between the main characters and their journey inside the Book of Everafter. Second, if you’re a Puckabrina lover, it’ll totally satisfy you! There are a bunch of Puckabrina moments in here that’ll make up for the slow torture it gave you from the past books! Though, I must say how Puckabrina ended in this book, is slightly disappointing. But still, it’s a good thing that Sabrina</span>
  <span id="freeText1148484311727023957" style="display:none">Ok, I have only one word to say about this book: Outstanding. First, there are a lot of suspense and thrilling moments between the main characters and their journey inside the Book of Everafter. Second, if you’re a Puckabrina lover, it’ll totally satisfy you! There are a bunch of Puckabrina moments in here that’ll make up for the slow torture it gave you from the past books! Though, I must say how Puckabrina ended in this book, is slightly disappointing. But still, it’s a good thing that Sabrina Grimm finally admitted Puck’s her first crush and kiss! XD But still… **sighs** they decided that they should change the future of them getting married to each other. Third, it’s very fun how they messed up each fairytale they got transported into. And every character fearing the Editor and the “revisers” and eventually ending up in their library and meeting them personally.<br />Out of all the fairy tales they ‘messed up’, my favourites will be The Wonderful World of Oz and Snow White. The Wonderful World of Oz for it’s so hilarious and humorous! Sabrina and Daphne kept doing things on the other way around like leaving the scarecrow, Tin Man and even making the Cowardly Lion unconscious! And when they were in front of the castle, they didn’t know how to get through and suddenly saw the three characters standing behind them, looking mad. Hahaha! :P My favorite part on that fairytale was when they met the Wicked Witch of the West and then Daphne/Dorothy doesn’t want to throw the pail of water to her. But the Witch begged and eventually, she just threw the bucket on her head and melted into a puddle. I remember the Editor said he doesn’t remember the Witch begging Dorothy to kill her! XD XD XD<br />On Snow White, well that was where they finally meet Mirror for the second time and saved their baby brother, Basil Grimm. But that’s not the reason why I love it. It’s because… **squeals like a fan girl** **takes a deep breath** ok… **takes another deep breath** It’s because… **squeals again** <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Sabrina kissed Puck!!!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. There I said it. She did that for Puck <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ ate the poisonous apple the Wicked Queen gave Snow White!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. So yeah, true love kiss can only wake him up. <br />Want to know the ending? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The Grimms saved their baby brother but Mirror possessed Granny Relda instead and fled from the story to the real world with Atticus, William’s evil brother, following after him. They went back to the real world and that was where Sabrina kissed Puck and he woke up. The two talked about their future and Sabrina explained that they’ll change it- which means they’ll try to not end up getting married! After that, Sabrina finally admitted she likes Puck and started planning to defeat Mirror first. The last scene was Daphne saying they needed to seek help with Baba Yaga. <br />For Puckabrina fans, here’s an excerpt from the scene where Sabrina kissed Puck and talked about their future:<br />“Well?” Daphne said to Sabrina. <br />“Well what?” <br />“Are you going to wake Puck up?”<br />“We tried,” Sabrina said. “He ate part of a poisoned apple.” <br />“Did you kiss him?”<br />Sabrina wasn’t sure she heard her sister correctly. <br />“What?”<br />“You have to kiss him. He needs the kiss of someone who loves him.” <br />“Absolutely not!” Henry shouted. <br />“It has to be a romantic kiss too,” Daphne added slyly. “Listen, he’s asleep, and if anyone knows about that spell it’s the Grimm family. If there is even the teensiest chance that you love Puck, you have to kiss him.”<br />“There’s no chance at all!” Sabrina said, wracking her brain for a really great excuse. “I don’t love him. It won’t work.”<br />“Then he’ll sleep forever,” Daphne said. <br />Sabrina looked at Puck. He was smelly, rude, mean, selfish, stupid, and immature. He wasn’t the kind of boy that girls fell in love with. He was the kind of boy you stayed fifty yards from at all times. Kissing him wouldn’t wake him up, but if everyone was going to pressure her, what else could she do? She’d kiss him and mentally reminded herself to brush, floss, and gargle the first chance she got. She looked to her father, who seemed physically ill, while her mother smiled reassuringly. Daphne rolled her eyes. “Geez, enough with the buildup. Just do it.” <br />Sabrina leaned in and pressed her lips to Puck’s. There was a little static shock that startled her and she stepped back with her hands on her mouth. <br />“Oh!” It hadn’t hurt. It was just… surprising. <br />Puck’s eyes flickered open and he looked around. “So, what did I miss?’<br />The family spent the rest of the day retrieving what little was left intact in the house. Even Pinocchio helped, albeit reluctantly. Most of the time he groused about “child labor laws” and “indentured servitude.” It gave Sabrina and Puck time to be alone. They sat in the yard and looked over the house for a while in silence. <br />Finally, Puck spoke. “Let’s not change.” <br />“Huh?”<br />“The insults. The pranks. Let’s not change.” <br />“I don’t know what you’re talking about.” <br />“Someday you and I are getting married.” Puck sighed, as if terribly depressed. “The cruel hand of fate will not allow us to escape it. Worse, my own body is betraying me. I’m getting older every day. So, in essence, we are up the river without a paddle. If we have to get married and have a million babies, I hope our relationship will be built on mutual disgust and an endless barrage of ridicule and insults. It feels like the only thing I can count on right now. I don’t want something dumb like respect and affection getting in the way.” <br />Sabrina laughed. “OK, on the outside chance that you and I do getting married, I promise to insult you all day long. But you do realize there’s a very good chance that you and I won’t get married.” <br />“That’s not what you told me. You said you went to the future and we were married,” Puck said. “We can’t escape fate.” <br />“We didn’t see the future. We saw a future,” Sabrina said. “The world we saw was terrible. The Master was in control of everything. Dragons hunted people. Human beings were refugees. When we got back to our time, Daphne and I started doing everything we could to prevent that from happening. And we have managed to change some stuff. For instance, Snow White was dead in the future but we saved her life. Daphne had a horrible scar on her face but we fixed that, too. There have been countless other things we stopped from happening. We may have altered the future so much that you and I don’t get married.” <br />Puck sat back, deep in thought. “So, you and I might not get married and have to do all that mushy stuff and have kids buy a house and get a mortgage? I might not have to get a job or take baths or take up reading?”<br />Sabrina shook her head. “If we rescue Granny Relda and stop Mirror for good, we could probably change it all.” <br />“Great! Let’s kick Mirror’s butt,” he said. <br />Sabrina smiled at the joke but down deep it hurt a little. Not that she wanted her whole life planned out for her when she was only twelve years old. She wanted there to be mysteries about the life she might lead and the loves she might find along the way, and she didn’t want fate telling her whom she was supposed to be with. Still, Puck was special to her. He was her first kiss; her first crush. <br />There was no use denying it anymore. Poisoned apples had spilled the beans. <br />“Thank you, Sabrina Grimm.” <br />“For what?”<br />“Don’t torture me! I won’t say it out loud. Just… you know, in four thousand years no one has felt… Oh, just forget it!” he said. He took a strong whiff of the air. “Geez, Grimm. You’re rank.” <br />Then he walked away.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br />That’s all!  Over all, I really enjoyed the book and can’t wait for the last one! XD </span>
  <a data-text-id="1148484311727023957" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_231168714" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/231168714" />
    <a title="Mara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6879652-mara"><img alt="Mara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380254226p2/6879652.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/231168714?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mara" href="/user/show/6879652-mara">Mara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6879652-mara?shelf=books-owned">books-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6879652-mara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6879652-mara?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6879652-mara?shelf=fairytale-retelling">fairytale-retelling</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer231168714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13789021543757663630">I've found this series funny and one of the cleverest "retellings" I've read in a long time. Most of the characters are annoying, especially Sabrina, but if you are a fan of fairy tales and like to read comedies based on them, then you can ignore these annoyances. Daphne is awesome, and Sabrina does get a little better after . . . five or six books. And the series definitely keeps you guessing once the main plot is introduced (which doesn't take long). That said, let us turn our attention to Boo</span>
  <span id="freeText13789021543757663630" style="display:none">I've found this series funny and one of the cleverest "retellings" I've read in a long time. Most of the characters are annoying, especially Sabrina, but if you are a fan of fairy tales and like to read comedies based on them, then you can ignore these annoyances. Daphne is awesome, and Sabrina does get a little better after . . . five or six books. And the series definitely keeps you guessing once the main plot is introduced (which doesn't take long). That said, let us turn our attention to Book Eight.<br /><br />I didn't hold too much hope for this one. Eight books is a lot, and authors can make fun of fairy tales for only so long. After reading Book Seven - The Everafter War - I was a little tired of them and dearly wishing Michael Buckley would stop, even though I was greatly impressed with Book Seven's twisty and unexpected ending. Who would have ever guessed that he would turn out to be the Master? I'm glad it took Mr. Buckley a year to write The Inside Story, otherwise I might have found this one tedious. But the rest did my perspective good, and even so there is no denying that this one was entertaining.<br /><br />As an author, I view characters in a much different manner than your day-to-day bookworm. They can be, and usually are, as real to me as any friend. They have their personalities, desires, bad days, and undying loyalty (or clever evilness, depending on what sort of character they are). An author may think they control their characters' fates, but meddle with their wishes too much and the characters may rebel. It is because of this that I found the situations involving the Editor and the characters in the Book of Everafter so hilarious and rather relateable (in a sense). The Editor thought he controlled the characters; he revised and revised as much as he wanted in order to keep the stories on track, but in the end some of the characters rebel and he has a hard time of keeping them from killing him. In reality, rebellious characters won't kill you (not usually), but they will leave your service, giving you nothing but an empty shell with their name. And trust me - readers notice when this happens.<br /><br />Over all, this was a fun adventure - following Sabrina and Daphne through various familiar fairy tales and seeing how they messed them up. A safe "what-if" scenario. I particularly liked what Michael Buckley did with the Snow White story. He introduces a concept that Snow White and the Seven Dwarfs wasn't always like it is now; that it was once a very dark, depressing, and dramatic story that was too dangerous to be kept that way, and it had to be revised. But the dangerous element could not simply be wiped away - it is still out there, desiring to be free.<br /><br />Fans of the The Sisters Grimm won't be disappointed. Especially with the hilarious situation between Puck and Sabrina, and the surprising end (though not nearly as surprising as The Everafter War). My only hope is that Michael Buckley will not drag this series out to a point where people just get sick to the teeth of it and quit. Buckley can get by with at least one more installment - possibly two more, but it will be stretching it. Any more and he will be hitting the dangerous zone.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13789021543757663630" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_103983199" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103983199" />
    <a title="Evy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3666631-evy"><img alt="Evy" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103983199?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evy" href="/user/show/3666631-evy">Evy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">9-11 year old kids with a good sense of imagination</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3666631-evy?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103983199" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11865156451276203368">Lately I've been reading child-relevant (that's the word they used on a website) books, which you can relate to. I love that genre but was definitely willing to put it down for Michael Buckley's THE INSIDE STORY. I have fallen in love with the series and couldn't wait to see the latest book. <br/>THE INSIDE STORY, once finished, was very revealing to many secrets and exactly what I expected...and then some. It was very exciting to read but with one flaw...: I believe that in all of Buckley's books so</span>
  <span id="freeText11865156451276203368" style="display:none">Lately I've been reading child-relevant (that's the word they used on a website) books, which you can relate to. I love that genre but was definitely willing to put it down for Michael Buckley's THE INSIDE STORY. I have fallen in love with the series and couldn't wait to see the latest book. <br />THE INSIDE STORY, once finished, was very revealing to many secrets and exactly what I expected...and then some. It was very exciting to read but with one flaw...: I believe that in all of Buckley's books so far he has explained the best parts the longest, yet with the 8th book of the Sisters Grimm series he hardly lengthened on the really interesting parts, for example where Granny Relda and the family mess up the books together. It was short and one-and-a-half pages, which was a bit disappointing. But otherwise, if you can live with it, this book is a great one.<br />Unlike the other Sisters Grimm series books, you really have to know each book's plot by heart in order to understand this one. You have to know, mainly, the plot of the seventh book and also the reason of this havoc in the eighth. So, therefore, if you are reading this review and are interested in the eighth book but have either not read any of or skipped some of the series, then you should immediately close this window, change your library requests to book 1, and start from there, because I assure you that if you just randomly pick up this book it would do you absolutely no good at all.<br />Sneak peek of the story below:<br /><br />Sabrina feels empty. Why? She has everything she's ever wanted for the past 2 years: her family back together again...and, well, a family to have. But that one chunk of her is missing. It's her baby brother. Mirror took off with Sammy (one of the names Daphne picks) into a book chock full of Everafters. It's risking their lives, but Sabrina, Daphne, and Puck jump into the book to follow him and Pinocchio. They must stop Mirror and Pinocchio, as they might change their story, therefore changing history. But they must also dodge the Editor and his revisers and the strange beast that are spoken of amongst the Everafters in the books. The 'thing' is hiding in the margins of the stories, and if they can't get Oohg (another name) back, they might as well be killed by the 'thing' and let their baby brother get consumed by Mirror. Oh, and one last thing, to Sabrina's dread. Puck WANTS to get married.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11865156451276203368" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_180312023" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/180312023" />
    <a title="Lynn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4193245-lynn"><img alt="Lynn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365094487p2/4193245.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/180312023?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynn" href="/user/show/4193245-lynn">Lynn</a>
      </span>

          marked it as listened-to-on-audiobook




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer180312023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7958063381716710135">In my humble opinion everyone should read Michael Buckley's Sisters Grimm series. It is just that good.<br/><br/>Sabrina, Daphne, and Puck have leapt into the Book of Everafter to stop Mirror and save their little brother. They must move from one story to another taking roles in the story and that is half the fun. Okay, what story will be next. With a sentence of a clue, can you figure out where they are before they state it?<br/><br/>The relationship between Puck and Sabrina is hilarious as it develops. The reader</span>
  <span id="freeText7958063381716710135" style="display:none">In my humble opinion everyone should read Michael Buckley's Sisters Grimm series. It is just that good.<br /><br />Sabrina, Daphne, and Puck have leapt into the Book of Everafter to stop Mirror and save their little brother. They must move from one story to another taking roles in the story and that is half the fun. Okay, what story will be next. With a sentence of a clue, can you figure out where they are before they state it?<br /><br />The relationship between Puck and Sabrina is hilarious as it develops. The reader knows that they really are good friends and they continue their rude comments of dog-face and stinky all through out, yet when push comes to shove and either needs help and support the other is there in amazing ways.<br /><br />I love the commentary about being a hero -- once when Sabrina is bemoaning her failures. Puck comes in with such wonderful insight that only a 12 year old boy who has been a boy for 4000 years could come up with. "You are not a failure, you are a hero and heroes have to overcome difficulty"<br /><br />I think nowadays many kids (and adults) forget who are real heroes. We see celebrities and sports stars and forget that they are rarely people we should want to emulate. Sabrina has her faults (many of them in fact) but she does her best to overcome her failures and pursue the good to help her family.<br /><br />This is just about the best series ever and I am so disappointed that there is only ONE more book left in the series!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7958063381716710135" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2272277-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1241102044p2/2272277.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103772890?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/2272277-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2272277-julie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2272277-julie?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103772890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2894177225504467363">I started reading this series and now I'm so far into it, that I'm stuck until it ends. (Please tell me it's going to end!)<br/><br/>Unfortunately, with the later books, I have a lot of trouble concentrating. This book was better than the last one in that respect, but still had its moments of 'get on with it already'. Except that getting on with it is sort of the problem.<br/><br/>There's a lot of plot and a lot of action, and my brain just shuts off. I suspect it's a boy type of story and I need more of a girl typ</span>
  <span id="freeText2894177225504467363" style="display:none">I started reading this series and now I'm so far into it, that I'm stuck until it ends. (Please tell me it's going to end!)<br /><br />Unfortunately, with the later books, I have a lot of trouble concentrating. This book was better than the last one in that respect, but still had its moments of 'get on with it already'. Except that getting on with it is sort of the problem.<br /><br />There's a lot of plot and a lot of action, and my brain just shuts off. I suspect it's a boy type of story and I need more of a girl type of story. I need more time to sit down with the characters. I need a slower pace. I need fewer things to happen and more reaction to the things that happen.<br /><br />Oh, I suppose I should say what the book is about. The Grimm girls are fairy tale detectives, and in this book they're chasing down a bad guy who's kidnapped their baby brother. And they're doing so in a sort of master book of stories. So they go to Oz and and Mowgli's Jungle and things like that.<br /><br />Which is an interesting premise that's not used to its full advantage. Or, well, maybe just not used how I would use it.<br /><br />Anyway, just as the story starts getting really interesting and good again.. it ends. To be continued in the next book.<br /><br />So. Sigh. Mostly I guess I'd recommend it to kids who like plot who want/need to read more with female main characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2894177225504467363" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15183804029575165825" style="display:none"> I recently read The sisters Grimm The inside story Book 8. There are 288 pages. It was published in 2010. The author is Michael Buckley. This book is intended for 5th to 9th graders,<br /> The main issue is they are trying to get there baby brother back. The setting is in a story book. The main characters are Sabrina. She is scared, mad, and annoyed. Daphne is joyful and happy. Puck is annoying, Sabrina’s fiancée, and he is stinky.<br /> They followed the master into a fairy-tale book. They try to rescue their baby brother from the master. While they are there they have to jump from fairy-tale to fairy-tale. Now they have to be careful or the editor with erase the book and everyone in it.<br /> I liked that they go their baby brother back. I didn’t like that the master jumped into one of the Grimm’s bodies. My favorite quote is “Keep your paws off my fiancée you flea-ridden stray.” Puck. <br /> The theme is if you mess with the master you will lose a family member. I recommend this book to those who like fairy-tales they jump from book to book. The unique thing about this book is that they revise something if the story did something wrong.<br /></span>

<div id="review_116182390" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/116182390" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/314910-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441555253p2/314910.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/116182390?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/314910-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer116182390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5900058277654304855">Another great Sisters Grimm book.<br/><br/>Starting out, I was a little confused by the book. The previous books in the series, I had read all at once, and that was months and months ago, so it took me a while to remember what exactly was going on and what had happened to different characters and who was who. I'm pretty sure that I finally got it all straight, but am not quite sure. <br/><br/>I really enjoyed the book, expecially as the characters went into some of my favorite books, such as The Wizard of Oz and Al</span>
  <span id="freeText5900058277654304855" style="display:none">Another great Sisters Grimm book.<br /><br />Starting out, I was a little confused by the book. The previous books in the series, I had read all at once, and that was months and months ago, so it took me a while to remember what exactly was going on and what had happened to different characters and who was who. I'm pretty sure that I finally got it all straight, but am not quite sure. <br /><br />I really enjoyed the book, expecially as the characters went into some of my favorite books, such as The Wizard of Oz and Alice's Adventures in Wonderland, but nothing seemed to really happen in the story. It was an entire book of not much actually occuring. I had thought that this would be the last book in the series, but I'm starting to wonder if it will ever end. I hope that Buckley does not drag it out too long. The series it good, but it's difficult having to wait so long before releases on a series that is already eight books along. Some things weren't meant to last forever--endings are a good thing.</span>

<div id="review_107377088" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107377088" />
    <a title="Kevin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/208149-kevin"><img alt="Kevin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605104785p2/208149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107377088?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kevin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kevin" href="/user/show/208149-kevin">Kevin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15599248750908558617">I am a big fan of this series but #8 struck me as a little thin in places. It has sort of postmodern perspective as the characters are stuck in The Book of Everafter chasing Pinochio and the Mirror through classic fairy tales while at the same time dealing with The Editor and his voracious revisors.<br/><br/>The focus is mostly on Sabrina as she comes to grip with being a leader for her family and friends and he developing relationship with Puck.<br/><br/>The ending picked up and there is still some funny lines and</span>
  <span id="freeText15599248750908558617" style="display:none">I am a big fan of this series but #8 struck me as a little thin in places. It has sort of postmodern perspective as the characters are stuck in The Book of Everafter chasing Pinochio and the Mirror through classic fairy tales while at the same time dealing with The Editor and his voracious revisors.<br /><br />The focus is mostly on Sabrina as she comes to grip with being a leader for her family and friends and he developing relationship with Puck.<br /><br />The ending picked up and there is still some funny lines and interactions but the middle was a little flat as they jumped from one story to the next. Could be the simplified story - that is after all for young readers - just didn't grab me this time.<br /><br />Still a great series and I will the read the next one I am sure.</span>

<div id="review_209527451" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/209527451" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6316340-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/209527451?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/6316340-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer209527451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4293808504254327358"><i>The Inside Story</i> is probably one of the best Sister Grimm books yet. With it's humerous dialog and plot line, stunning character growth, and amazing twists and turns this book is a must read. From the moment I picked up the book I couldn't put it down.<br/><br/>If someone came up to me and asked me to describe this book in three words I probably; "So freaking epic" as a response. Because this book really was that. If someone asked me to give them my three favorite things about this book I'd say; "The roma</span>
  <span id="freeText4293808504254327358" style="display:none"><i>The Inside Story</i> is probably one of the best Sister Grimm books yet. With it's humerous dialog and plot line, stunning character growth, and amazing twists and turns this book is a must read. From the moment I picked up the book I couldn't put it down.<br /><br />If someone came up to me and asked me to describe this book in three words I probably; "So freaking epic" as a response. Because this book really was that. If someone asked me to give them my three favorite things about this book I'd say; "The romance, the humor, and the adventures". While this book wasn't as funny as <i>The Everafter War</i> (which for some reason people didn't like too much) it was still pretty darn funny. Daphne really made me laugh with her suggestions for the names for the baby (Oogh was my personal favorite). <br /><br />Mr. Buckley, I would like to thank you for <i>finally</i> making Sabrina less grumpy. It was nice to see her be like this. Some people said it made her weak-but I think it made her human. <br /><br />Okay, I really loved Puck nicknames for Sabrina through-out this book. They were extrememly epic. Especailly her reaction to said nicknames. <br /><br />There is one part of this story that I must tell you about so bewarned there are spoilers ahead! <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Finally! She sort of admits her feelings towards Puck. And they kiss. And no one got punched this time! Daphne you were amazing for making this kiss be true by telling Sabrina to kiss him. Seriously. It was amazing. Okay, end of me being a fangirl. But they better get back together in the next book(since the series is ending) or I will be one angry fangirl.<br /><br />~Alyssa~ <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_481540117" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/481540117" />
    <a title="Anis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12782187-anis"><img alt="Anis" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/481540117?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anis" href="/user/show/12782187-anis">Anis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer481540117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4620825390818681257">Moving on, The 8th Book is so speechless of words to say how amazing it is! I keep saying these words because it really was soo fun to read them. It made me feel as if I was still reading the books from book one till book 5 which is good because were near the end of the series and its good to have a good knack of going through the past with them to have feel that rush of adrenaline and experience you have with them before you have to say goodbye :'(<br/><br/>Honestly, reading this book was feeling like yo</span>
  <span id="freeText4620825390818681257" style="display:none">Moving on, The 8th Book is so speechless of words to say how amazing it is! I keep saying these words because it really was soo fun to read them. It made me feel as if I was still reading the books from book one till book 5 which is good because were near the end of the series and its good to have a good knack of going through the past with them to have feel that rush of adrenaline and experience you have with them before you have to say goodbye :'(<br /><br />Honestly, reading this book was feeling like your a real adventurer and you can see everything that's going on. One again the awkward love connections with Puck and Sabrina just became more cuter and even better to imagine! How Puck teases her and how he knew that they were going to get married that he even called her names such as 'honey boo' or 'fiancee' too cute! And its sot of sad how the end gets getting even closer and closer. The adventure sort of became too mainstream because they just keep being in the boo of EverAfter all the time but I looked at the positive side and saw that its one last fun journey before the end.<br /><br />One of the reading strategies that helped me were visualizing because some moments that would have been too shocking would have been better If I have seen it myself visually. I tend to use this particular strategy in the Puck and Sabrina moments because they were so unusual just to read it that I sort of had to visualize it and see how it really went. <br /><br />Overall, this book stole all of my great comments so I would give this book a 10/10 for the creativity and the broad storyline with the drama, romance and events that happens which make it so exciting! Off to the 9th book! :) <br /><br /></span>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1002421238?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie" href="/user/show/9320233-stephanie">Stephanie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1002421238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4434098180495550662">Even though this series is decidedly PG, I have to admit I quite liked it. Excellent premise, well-planned character development, good writing. <br/>There were some minor frustrations, but the characters and subplots were great, so I kept coming back to find out what happened in the end. <br/><br/>The bad points: <br/>1) The heroes in the book are often quite oblivious. Sabrina is 12, so being staggeringly foolish now and then can be excused, but for characters who have lived hundreds (or thousands) of years, I'd e</span>
  <span id="freeText4434098180495550662" style="display:none">Even though this series is decidedly PG, I have to admit I quite liked it. Excellent premise, well-planned character development, good writing. <br />There were some minor frustrations, but the characters and subplots were great, so I kept coming back to find out what happened in the end. <br /><br />The bad points: <br />1) The heroes in the book are often quite oblivious. Sabrina is 12, so being staggeringly foolish now and then can be excused, but for characters who have lived hundreds (or thousands) of years, I'd expect a little wisdom.<br /> <br />2) Personally, I think it would have been easier to buy in to the story with a little more realism/consistency . . . <br /> a. Though the internet is mentioned, no one seems to have access to it in Fairyport Landing. Ditto for cell phones. Really? In 2013?<br /><br /> b. Yes, I know these are YA books, but we're supposed to believe no one in this town (including a 12 year old from Manhattan who lived in the foster system for 2 years) EVER swears? Not even a "damn"? <br /><br />Overall, it was a good series. Definitely worth reading, even if it was a bit predictable. <br /><br />*I'd like to note that my husband had a GREAT prediction for the ending (SPOILER ALERT), and I was actually disappointed that the author didn't think of it . . . <br />My hubby thought that, at the wedding, Bradley was going to turn out to be Puck in disguise. The idea being that he'd pretended to be this very normal human for years, duping Sabrina into marrying him when she said she'd never do it. Then he sprouts wings at the altar and reveals that this is his ultimate prank. Tah-dah! Wouldn't that be so Puck? <br /> <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4434098180495550662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I got through about 200 pages, but I just can't go any further. I'm not sure why, but with each successive book, Sabrina just gets on my nerves a little more. I will not be finishing this series, and I honestly wish I'd quit several books ago.</span>

<div id="review_1341147555" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1341147555" />
    <a title="Anushka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5566247-anushka"><img alt="Anushka" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1341147555?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anushka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anushka" href="/user/show/5566247-anushka">Anushka</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5566247-anushka?shelf=catalogued">catalogued</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1341147555&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1341147555" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9595610577344238236">Find this and the rest of my reviews of the Sisters Grimm series at Feminist Quill.Wordpress: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://feministquill.wordpress.com/2015/12/19/book-review-the-sisters-grimm-7-9/'>https://feministquill.wordpress.com/2...</a><br/><br/>SERIOUS AND MAJOR SPOILERS (Especially for Book 9) INCLUDED.<br/>Don't even think about reading this book unless you don't care about spoilers. <br/><br/>Also, REALLY long review. Sorry, but there was a LOT to rant about.<br/><br/>Plot Description: The final three books in this series are darker, edgier, and the plots get more wilder and implausible than ever. To add to this mess, there's</span>
  <span id="freeText9595610577344238236" style="display:none">Find this and the rest of my reviews of the Sisters Grimm series at Feminist Quill.Wordpress: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://feministquill.wordpress.com/2015/12/19/book-review-the-sisters-grimm-7-9/">https://feministquill.wordpress.com/2...</a><br /><br />SERIOUS AND MAJOR SPOILERS (Especially for Book 9) INCLUDED.<br />Don't even think about reading this book unless you don't care about spoilers. <br /><br />Also, REALLY long review. Sorry, but there was a LOT to rant about.<br /><br />Plot Description: The final three books in this series are darker, edgier, and the plots get more wilder and implausible than ever. To add to this mess, there's more sexism and problematic plot points, story lines that drag on forever, and TERRIBLE editing and continuity issues. <br />To summarize, The Everafter War deals with a Civil War between factions led by Charming and the Queen of Hearts respectively. Oh, and the children's parents are finally awake - which is not the good thing I was hoping it would be. The Big Bad is finally revealed, and while this reveal is impressive at first, I was progressively less impressed and more annoyed by the Master's plan, motivations, minions... everything. <br />The Inside Story is a bizarre and completely meta journey through the original book with which the fates of all the Everafters are entwined. Sabrina and Daphne follow the Master through all the fairytale stories as they try to stop the Master from rewriting their story. <br />The Council of Mirrors features the final showdown/ battles/ curses et cetera et cetera. It also features what was possibly the most random subplot; inserted as the most random plot twist ever, and about which I'm completely conflicted. <br /><br />While Sabrina and Daphne are finally beginning to show signs of solid character development, the appearance of their parents on the scene kind of sets the whole family back by about ten steps. To be more specific, it turns out the girls' dad is a controlling idiot who won't listen to reason, doesn't consider his daughters' opinions worth listening to despite everything they've achieved so far, and follows a policy of requiring strict obedience. Including from his wife. <br />Suddenly, the girls' mother getting involved with the Faerie in NYC is put into greater perspective. She went to great lengths to keep her activities secret even though she was standing up for something she believed in - all because her husband will throw a temper tantrum and 'forbid' her from doing things he doesn't like. <br /><br />[Full disclosure: The girls' father is only unreasonable when it comes to Everafters, and that's because he watched his father die because of them/ at their hands or something else. This, however, does not excuse a grown man for dragging his family out into the woods in the midst of a war, with NO plan, NO money or supplies, and NO agenda except for 'you're all supposed to just listen to me'. ]<br /><br />One of the characters in the book tries a retcon justification for his behaviour by calling him the 'protector' of the family. But dude, no.<br /><br />I think this nonsense about confusing protection (and the affection that comes with it) with the need to control people needs to stop, and it needs to stop NOW. Too many fathers and other kinds of paternalistic figures have justified the most unacceptable kinds of behaviour by claiming that they were acting in the best interests of their dependents. And this is despite the fact that in a LOT of these cases, their behaviour when evaluated from an objective perspective was found to NOT to be in the best interests of their dependents.<br /><br />Clearly Mr. Grimm isn't the only person to ever have engaged in such nonsense behaviour, and he certainly won't be the last... but let's not confuse protection with control, and let's not ignore this issue. <br /><br />From an objective plot perspective, The Inside Story is convoluted and largely unnecessary. It's clear by this point that the story is being stretched as thin as it can be without it falling apart. <br /><br />But I won't deny that The Inside Story was kind of fun to read. It's every reader's fantasy to be able to step into their favourite books and get to enact parts of it out - maybe even change stuff around. To suddenly be the star of your favourite show - that's what this book is all about. <br /><br />And that brings us to The Council of Mirrors and an end to this whole... experience (for lack of a nicer word). The final scenes of the story involve Snow White - a character who has always been a part of the story without really taking centre stage at any point of it. Her on-off relationship with Charming is one of the running gags throughout the stories. Snow is someone who actively works to shed herself of the damsel in distress tag - she's a Ferryport self defence instructor, and she refuses to allow Charming's self absorption to define her or their relationship. <br />In the final plot, it is revealed that the story of Snow White has been faked - it wasn't the version included in the original Grimm stories. In the real version, she's married off to a sadistic and abusive husband, at whose hands she dies. Unable to watch her daughter's life play out in this manner over and over again, her mother - the Evil Queen - steps in to modify the story and edit the abusive husband out of it (replacing him with herself as the villain instead). Charming, the sadistic Prince's younger brother, was written into the story as Snow's love interest, and that was that. <br /><br />Or it would have been, if Sabrina and Daphne (and the Master) hadn't crashed through the Fairytale book in which he had been trapped, and freed him. In a final showdown between this man and Charming, (after Snow has been kidnapped and taken away as the guy's lawful wife - and property), he's finally overpowered. It took like, a bunch of people to get the job done. And then Snow delivers the killing stroke - and with that action supposedly reclaims her identity and her life. <br /><br />Heavy stuff, huh. At first I felt it a little inappropriate - introducing such a horrible sub plot into what's essentially a book for children. But then I remembered that the original tales by the real brothers Grimm had been graphic, gory and ugly. <br /><br />This evocation of the spirit of the original tales - be it conscious or unconscious - seems to be a theme in the Sisters Grimm series. I was discussing Sleeping Beauty a few days ago, and we were talking about how in the original story, the Prince rapes her in her sleep, causing her to become pregnant and to deliver twins - whilst still asleep. She only woke up when one of the twins accidentally sucked the cursed flax/ needle out of her finger. <br /><br />At the time, I couldn't remember where I'd read something similar. At least, not until I began reviewing books 4 - 6 of this series. The girls' mother, Veronica, is pregnant at the time when she's kidnapped by the Master along with her husband and put into an enchanted sleep for two years. She delivers the baby while in her sleep - because yes, THAT'S how childbirth works. (I don't know why he didn't just throw a stork in there too, just for kicks.)<br /><br />I mentioned in my review of Books 1 - 3 that I had issues with the subtextual messages being sent by this series. In addition to the conflation of protection and controlling &amp; my issues with this trivializing of subjects like childbirth and murder (remember the juvenile homicidal maniacs from book 2?), I find the way Snow White's story was resolved extremely problematic. <br /><br />For one thing, that entire subplot was completely unnecessary to the plot - the homicidal husband was never a part of the Master's plan - so clearly it was thrown in there because Buckley thought this a masterful retelling of the story on his part. Now, I've mentioned that he has managed to that very thing with the story of Little Red Riding Hood earlier. <br />But whatever worked for that subplot does NOT work for this one. For one thing, trauma is not easily or instantaneously gotten over. If years of training herself hasn't helped her yet, putting a knife through a man she didn't even help overpower is not going to do it. Life's not that easy, and if you're going to try and make it "realistic" for the kids by including homicidal husband storylines, then you really ought not to pull a last minute cop out and wrap it up neatly in a very unrealistic bow. <br /><br />The final three books in the Sisters Grimm bring a series that started out promising to a very disappointing (and badly edited) finish. The story was dragged out unnecessarily, and at times, it felt like the only thing keeping Buckley's universe together was a thin strand of fiction - which is the only thing every character and subplot in this series have in common after all. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9595610577344238236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3199288751" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3199288751" />
    <a title="Jennifer Dai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/102935033-jennifer-dai"><img alt="Jennifer Dai" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3199288751?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Dai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Dai" href="/user/show/102935033-jennifer-dai">Jennifer Dai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3199288751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6091719329828844983">Chioce book 2 Quarter 3<br/><br/>Book: The Siters Grimm-The inside story is a fantasy book written by Michael Buckley<br/><br/>The setting: The story takes place in Ferryport Landing New York. ((Spoiler-ish) The story takes place inside a book and that book is laocted in Ferryport Landing New York)<br/><br/>The main characters: The main characters in this book are Sabrina a 12 year old girl and her little sister named Daphne, who is 7 years old. (Maybe 7 and a half) I think that Sabrina is a dynamic character because in the </span>
  <span id="freeText6091719329828844983" style="display:none">Chioce book 2 Quarter 3<br /><br />Book: The Siters Grimm-The inside story is a fantasy book written by Michael Buckley<br /><br />The setting: The story takes place in Ferryport Landing New York. ((Spoiler-ish) The story takes place inside a book and that book is laocted in Ferryport Landing New York)<br /><br />The main characters: The main characters in this book are Sabrina a 12 year old girl and her little sister named Daphne, who is 7 years old. (Maybe 7 and a half) I think that Sabrina is a dynamic character because in the begining of the series she's always sure of her decigens and she never really gave her little sister an opinion in things, but now she's considering her sister's opinions and she's having a hard time deciding what’s right or wrong and making decisions. I think that Daphne is also an dynamic character because in the beginning of the series she was always happy and a little careless, also most childish, but now she’s way more mature and she helps her sister (Sabrina) a lot more. Another character is Puck, Puck is over 4 thousand years old, but his age in appearance is about the same age as Sabrina. I think Puck is also a dynamic character just like Sabrina and Daphne, because in the beginning of the series he tried to kill Sabrina and her sister, but later on he helped them and protected them, but he had always been teasing Sabrina, calling her names and pulling pranks on her, but now he’s considering Sabrina’s feelings treating her with a lot more respect and...he has a crush on her. <br /><br />The main problem/conflict: The problem in this story is that Mirror (one of Sabrina’s family’s closest and most trusted friend) turns out to be their greatest enemy and he’s attempting steal the body of Sabrina’s baby brother in order to be free because Mirror is an everafter and all everafters are trapped in Ferryport Landing. His ally Pinocchio is trying to change his past using the book of everafter which has the power to change history and it’s just very dangerous. In the process of trying to change his past he messes with the past of a number of other everafters. Sabrina, Daphne and Puck, together with the Editor (Editor, he’s sort of like the ‘guardian’ of the book of everafters) and his revisors (creatures who help him rewrite things in the book that weren’t a part of the story) chases after Pinocchio from story to story. (Spoiler) Then Mirror’s plans of taking Sabrina’s little brother’s body fails and he ends of taking the body of Granny Relda (Sabrina’s grandmother) and now he has disappeared with Sabrina’s grandmother. I think this problem is person vs person because Mirror is a person (sort of) and Sabrina and her family are also people and their going against each other.<br /><br />The theme: The author believes that your friends/family will be there to help you when you are having a hard time. (Text evidence #1) When Sabrina was having trouble deciding whether or not she should let Mirror go since he was holding people hostage, Daphne stepped in and helped her out. (Text evidence #2) When Sabrina, Daphne and Puck lost track of Mirror, Granny Relda and Sabrina’s parents arrived just in time to help. (Text evidence #3) When Sabrina was really stressed and pressured about making big decisions Puck took over and Sabrina was able to take a break.<br /><br />Opinion and analysis section: I enjoyed thus book because it filled in the cliffhanger from the last book, even though it left on ANOTHER cliffhanger!!!(which the book didn’t feel complete) But cliffhangers he’ll keep the readers wanting to read the series. My favorite part of the book was when Puck kicked Pinocchio in the behind sending him flying through a magic door face first. If I were the author I wouldn’t have done anything differently. Compared to all the other books I’ve read in this series I think this book would be sort of in the middle, I love it, but I don’t love it that much.</span>

<div id="review_2415789681" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2415789681" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11114567-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590616772p2/11114567.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2415789681?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/11114567-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11114567-hannah?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2415789681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1010036917901281256">Okay, I’ve been really critical of this series. As far as children’s books go, this probably deserves five stars. But I can’t give them ALL five stars, right?<br/><br/>I like the development of the characters, first of all. Sabrina’s emotions are engaging to watch, as are Puck’s. Unfortunately, it makes me uncomfortable to be supposed to be shipping them. They’re twelve, guys! That said, these books do have a tendency to take mature thought towards normally lightly treated ideas. <br/><br/>The plot itself was great</span>
  <span id="freeText1010036917901281256" style="display:none">Okay, I’ve been really critical of this series. As far as children’s books go, this probably deserves five stars. But I can’t give them ALL five stars, right?<br /><br />I like the development of the characters, first of all. Sabrina’s emotions are engaging to watch, as are Puck’s. Unfortunately, it makes me uncomfortable to be supposed to be shipping them. They’re twelve, guys! That said, these books do have a tendency to take mature thought towards normally lightly treated ideas. <br /><br />The plot itself was great. I love the twists that must have been planned the entire time. Mirror makes a great villain, and once again they have a mature take on the moral ambiguity. Unlike young adult novels, they do not overlinger on whether the villain is right, which is a really, really good thing. <br /><br />The thing that took it down from a five stars is mostly because the plot got a little bogged down in the middle. It seemed kind of repetitive and not incredibly productive as they ran through the story. Just maybe they tried to cram in as many characters as possible? I’m not sure. <br /><br />Anyway, for a children’s story, it was great. I’m excited to read the last one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1010036917901281256" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The girls (and Puck) must chase the Master through a series of stories, where they’re willing to change what they need in order to save their baby brother. Soon, however, they are confronted by the Editor—the book’s guardian—who, along with an army of tiny monsters known as Revis</span>
  <span id="freeText7441362098073378487" style="display:none">After the shocking ending of The Everafter War, this book picks up with Sabrina, Daphne, and Puck stuck in the Book of Everafter, where all the fairy tales are stored and enchanted characters can change their destinies. The girls (and Puck) must chase the Master through a series of stories, where they’re willing to change what they need in order to save their baby brother. Soon, however, they are confronted by the Editor—the book’s guardian—who, along with an army of tiny monsters known as Revisers, threatens the children with dire consequences if they don’t stick to the stories. As they chase their quarry and dodge the Revisers, they meet Alice, Mowgli, Jack the Giant Killer, Hansel and Gretel, the Headless Horseman, and more. But will they find their brother in time?</span>

  <span id="freeText10128294332453727220" style="display:none">Daphne and Sabrina Grimm once again face a world of fairy tale creations, however, this time there is a difference. They know who the Master is and they're determined to get their little brother back o matter the cost. <br /><br />I loved this book Sabrina's crisis of confidence I feel is so important in her relationship with Daphne, and also with Puck. There are plot twists and turns, characters are introduced in a manner that still allows you to wonder what is occurring. I think this is one of my favourite ways that the Grimm Fairy Tales have ever been retold - Buckley cleverly acknowledges the different versions and works this to his advantage.</span>

<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25879858-charmed"><img alt="Charmed (Fairy Tale Reform School, #2)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1445423409l/25879858._SX98_.jpg" />

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lfqUMld9Mxn8WJhAxYB5NmizVBSa0do7T6ptYKmJlH1ufkFQLAKNvXNbD56+ho88e3ms5Ipb2FEfebwjhiwCVA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2HTlG5zDQxt+SE/l7jseFNBpKSP3fqvh5clHgJSFU1kj8DB557z9v/FL2DuVPegew6PR0+f0qYu1GpbDuyDFcA==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9981264258440052276">New York Times bestselling author Michael Buckley was born in Akron, Ohio. He tried his hand as a stand-up comic and lead singer for a punk rock back before attending Ohio University. After graduating with honors he moved to New York City to be an intern on the Late Show with David Letterman which led to stints developing programming for Discovery Networks, MTV, MTV Animation and Klasky Csupo (pro</span>
  <span id="freeText9981264258440052276" style="display:none">New York Times bestselling author Michael Buckley was born in Akron, Ohio. He tried his hand as a stand-up comic and lead singer for a punk rock back before attending Ohio University. After graduating with honors he moved to New York City to be an intern on the Late Show with David Letterman which led to stints developing programming for Discovery Networks, MTV, MTV Animation and Klasky Csupo (producers of Nickelodeon’s Rugrats). Today he lives in Brooklyn, New York with his wife, Alison, and their son Finn. <br /><br /><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217-master-list-of-author-disambiguation-by-spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information.</a></i> </span>
  <a data-text-id="9981264258440052276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    i = 0,
    go = function () {
      for (i = 0; i < n; i += 1) {
        script = d.createElement('SCRIPT');
        script.type = 'text/javascript';
        script.async = true;
        script.src = load[i];
        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }
    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>
